<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11159623005538267302">"Good gracious!" said Alice, "I do believe I'm inside a review!"<br/><br/>She turned to the Hatter and the March Hare. <br/><br/>"Well, let me see. Here is the title, and here is the date I read it. That must be today. Now I need to explain the plot and the overall point."<br/><br/>"There is no plot," said the March Hare disagreeably.<br/><br/>"And there is no point," agreed the Hatter. <br/><br/>He poured a little hot tea on the Dormouse's nose, making it wake with a start. <br/><br/>"The book breaks new ground," it said rapidly in a high, sing-song voi</span>
  <span id="freeText11159623005538267302" style="display:none">"Good gracious!" said Alice, "I do believe I'm inside a review!"<br /><br />She turned to the Hatter and the March Hare. <br /><br />"Well, let me see. Here is the title, and here is the date I read it. That must be today. Now I need to explain the plot and the overall point."<br /><br />"There is no plot," said the March Hare disagreeably.<br /><br />"And there is no point," agreed the Hatter. <br /><br />He poured a little hot tea on the Dormouse's nose, making it wake with a start. <br /><br />"The book breaks new ground," it said rapidly in a high, sing-song voice. "Intentionally eluding easy assignment to any traditional category, it anticipates the twentieth century's fascination with the relationship between the signifier and the signified, and wittily deconstructs the primacy of meaning and the rationality of thought." Then it went back to sleep again, and began to snore gently.<br /><br />"Whatever did that mean?" asked Alice, surprised.<br /><br />"Why is a Derrida like a derrière?" replied the Hatter.<br /><br />"I don't know," said Alice.<br /><br />"I don't know either," said the Hatter triumphantly.<br /><br />"It would be <i>reasonable</i>", said Alice, in the grown-up tone she had sometimes heard her sister use, "It would be <i>reasonable</i> for you to explain what the book is about, so that I could put that in my review." <br /><br />"It would be <i>reasonable</i>," said the Hatter, "to expect hot premarital sex in a Stephenie Meyer novel. But don't imagine you'll find any."<br /><br />Alice couldn't think of anything to reply to this, so she turned away without another word. When she was almost out of earshot, she thought she heard the Hatter shout something after her that might have been "Foucault!"<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1928668674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1928668674" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1928668674?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780147515872" href="/book/show/24611820-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=alice">alice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=i-love-these-characters">i-love-these-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1928668674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11377564548663305544">when I find myself in times of trouble<br/>Lewis Carroll comes to me<br/>speaking words of wisdom<br/>"just reread"<br/><br/>------------<br/><br/>THIS IS MY FAVORITE BOOK.<br/><br/>No qualifier. No excuse. No “one of my favorites.” This one is <i>it</i>, y’all.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/07/20/alices-adventures-in-wonderland-review-my-favorite-book-everrrr/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>Well, also Through the Looking Glass. But THAT’S PRACTICALLY THE SECOND HALF OF THE SAME BOOK. (And other examples of my inability to make decisions or commit in any way to anything.)<br/><br/>I currently have 18 copies of this book. I’ve attempted to read it </span>
  <span id="freeText11377564548663305544" style="display:none">when I find myself in times of trouble<br>Lewis Carroll comes to me<br>speaking words of wisdom<br>"just reread"<br><br>------------<br><br>THIS IS MY FAVORITE BOOK.<br><br>No qualifier. No excuse. No “one of my favorites.” This one is <i>it</i>, y’all.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/07/20/alices-adventures-in-wonderland-review-my-favorite-book-everrrr/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>Well, also Through the Looking Glass. But THAT’S PRACTICALLY THE SECOND HALF OF THE SAME BOOK. (And other examples of my inability to make decisions or commit in any way to anything.)<br><br>I currently have 18 copies of this book. I’ve attempted to read it at least annually for the past three years. And by “annually,” I mean I last revisited this book about nine months ago.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499528226ra/23242728.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But hey, it was a different year then, technically speaking.<br><br>How do I even review this? I don’t know where to begin. (Just a heads up that my obsessive personality is going to become verrrrry clear as this review progresses. I’m not proud. This is who I am, you guys. I was a member of the fandoms of some teen pop sensation or other for nearly ten consecutive years. I’m no longer thirteen but I still need an outlet. Honestly I’m quite afraid that if I don’t have an obsession, I’ll become a drug addict. Lots of pent up energy.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499528226ra/23242729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, I’ll say that I always, always, always feel enveloped by this book. I have never picked this up without feeling instantly submersed in Wonderland. And it’s really my favorite place to be. It’s hard to feel unhappy when you’re in the greatest setting ever created.<br><br>And oh yeah, there’s that. I firmly believe this is the most amazing and beautiful and confusing and curious setting of all time. It’s immersive, and it’s strange, and it’s so unique and fantastic and creative and I love it so much. I can come up with even more loosely positive adjectives if that overwhelming number didn’t suffice.<br><br>Wonderland is my Hogwarts. While many readers pray their letters just got lost in the mail, I’m constantly hoping I’ll see a white rabbit in a waistcoat and fall down, down, down into what must be the center of the earth.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456281365ra/18213534.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Alice and her curiosity. She may also be my favorite character ever. She’s funny and sweet and childish and such a blast to read about. Her reactions to everything are so, so funny. Her curiosity always outweighs confusion and fear. I’d like to wake up one day and <i>be</i> Alice. I’ll likely become one of those creeps who pays millions for plastic surgery in order to “resemble” some celebrity or other.<br><br>On an unrelated note, anyone have millions of dollars they’re trying to get rid of?<br><br>I’m also fiercely protective of this book. I constantly pick up retellings only to be utterly disappointed. (Like Heartless. Get <i>out</i> of here with your shoddy Carroll-stealing.) DO NOT, DO NOT! GET ME STARTED ON THE TIM BURTON FILM ADAPTATION. Horrific. Alice, an adult? Alice, engaged? Alice FIGHTING THE GODDAMN JABBERWOCK?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499528226ra/23242730.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I do love the original animated Disney adaptation. There’s a certain quality to the book that’s captured within that film, which I haven’t found recreated in any other retelling or use of the setting or adaptation.<br><br>Oh, and one more thing, while I’m here.<br><br>THIS BOOK ISN’T ABOUT DRUGS, YOU SURFACE-LEVEL INTERPRETERS OF SYMBOLISM. It’s not that easy, boo.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499528226ra/23242731.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the words of BBC News, “[the drug] references may say more about the people making them than the author.”<br><br>Lewis Carroll isn’t thought to have been a user of drugs, the Caterpillar was smoking tobacco, and the mushroom is no more magic than the various cakes Alice eats.<br><br>Honestly, the drug reading is simple and boring. It’s such a stretch to attempt to read each character as a different substance. And scrolling through countless quasi-psychedelic GIFs to find the actual ones was irritating, too. Ah, yes, real art: taking images from a 1951 children’s film but messing with the colors and movement until it looks like nothing more than a trigger for epilepsy. Enough, Tumblr.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458846670ra/18539035.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alice in Wonderland carries as much or as little significance as you want it to. It’s everything from a mindless romp in an imaginative land to a depiction of the effects of a ruthlessly authoritarian system of justice. <br><br>Just have fun with it.<br><br>And please, for the love of God, stop applying your weird psychedelic edits to a Disney movie.<br><br>Note on the audiobook: This time around, I listened to the audiobook, to switch things up. Scarlett Johansson read it. I loved her funny accents and hated her overly-acted narration. A mixed bag.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499528226ra/23242732.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line: This is my favoritest and I doubt it will be dethroned anytime soon. Come at me, every other book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11377564548663305544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2335236205?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688110871" href="/book/show/83345.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ye-old-bois">ye-old-bois</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2335236205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8344690623816883467"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595113227i/29838287._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote>Old books get a bad rap...but do they deserve it? Check out my latest <b>
  <u>
    <a href='https://youtu.be/LGrStFfbGmQ' rel='nofollow noopener'>BooktTube Video </a>
  </u>
</b> - all about the fabulous (and not so fabulous) Olde Boies.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><br/><br/><b> I should've read this one sooner </b> <blockquote>
  <i>“But I don’t want to go among mad people," Alice remarked.<br/>"Oh, you can’t help that," said the Cat: "we’re all mad here. I’m mad. You’re mad."</i>
</blockquote>I needed an <b>adequate amount of nostalgia</b> to guide me through this level of crazy. <blockquote>
  <i>Little Alice fell <br/>d<br/>o<br/>w<br/>n<br/>the hole, <br/>bumped her head<br/>and b</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8344690623816883467" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595113227i/29838287._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>Old books get a bad rap...but do they deserve it? Check out my latest <b>
  <u>
    <a href="https://youtu.be/LGrStFfbGmQ" rel="nofollow noopener">BooktTube Video </a>
  </u>
</b> - all about the fabulous (and not so fabulous) Olde Boies.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><br><br><b> I should've read this one sooner </b> <blockquote>
  <i>“But I don’t want to go among mad people," Alice remarked.<br>"Oh, you can’t help that," said the Cat: "we’re all mad here. I’m mad. You’re mad."</i>
</blockquote>I needed an <b>adequate amount of nostalgia</b> to guide me through this level of crazy. <blockquote>
  <i>Little Alice fell <br>d<br>o<br>w<br>n<br>the hole, <br>bumped her head<br>and bruised her soul!</i>
</blockquote>Everyone <b>knows this story</b>. Alice falls down the rabbit hole and into Wonderland - a place wholly unexpected, trivial and unforgettable. She meets several good friends (like the White Rabbit and the Cheshire Cat) and a few enemies (The Red Queen) as she stumbles her way through.<br><br>Reading this book for the first time as an adult leaves me <b>bewildered, vaguely amused and mostly lost.</b> I'm now worrying whether <b>I'm too old for children's stories anymore</b> (I briefly reread some of my faves - HP, Winnie the Pooh and Charlotte's Web - and have concluded it's not me, just that book).<br><br><b>It's all so illogical and confusing.</b> Alice (and everyone else in this novel) constantly contradicts themselves and each other. The whole thing is utter nonsense! Though, there are a few good puns: <blockquote>
  <i>No wise fish would go anywhere without a porpoise.</i>
</blockquote> Ah well. I will try it again some day just to see if <b>I was being a grump</b> on the day I read it and I plan to read this to my future-kids to see if their youth will allow them to interpret this more positively. After all, if Ronan Lynch from [Book: The Raven Boys] loves it then I will force myself too.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br> Read by Alan Bennett - and he was a pretty good narrator too. But as much as l I tried to listen to this on audiobook, the text was just tooo confusing. I kept losing track of the story. I gave up and decided to read it instead. That was a good choice - lots of fun pictures!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9778678194750159591">868.	Alice’s Adventures In Wonderland, Lewis Carroll<br/><br/>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland (commonly shortened to Alice in Wonderland) is an 1865 novel written by English author Charles Lutwidge Dodgson over the pseudonym Lewis Carroll. <br/><br/>It tells of a girl named Alice falling through a rabbit hole into a fantasy world populated by peculiar, anthropomorphic creatures. <br/><br/>The tale plays with logic, giving the story lasting popularity with adults as well as with children. It is considered to be one of the be</span>
  <span id="freeText9778678194750159591" style="display:none">868.	Alice’s Adventures In Wonderland, Lewis Carroll<br /><br />Alice's Adventures in Wonderland (commonly shortened to Alice in Wonderland) is an 1865 novel written by English author Charles Lutwidge Dodgson over the pseudonym Lewis Carroll. <br /><br />It tells of a girl named Alice falling through a rabbit hole into a fantasy world populated by peculiar, anthropomorphic creatures. <br /><br />The tale plays with logic, giving the story lasting popularity with adults as well as with children. It is considered to be one of the best examples of the literary nonsense genre. <br /><br />Its narrative course and structure, characters and imagery have been enormously influential in both popular culture and literature, especially in the fantasy genre.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: در سال 1974میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: آلیس در سرزمین عجایب؛ نویسنده: لوئیس کارول؛ مترجم: ایرج غریب؛ تهران، امیرکبیر، کتابهای طلایی، چاپ چهارم 1353؛ در 27ص؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 19م<br /><br />مترجمها: (احمد پناهی خراسانی، در سال 1371، در 159ص؛ مشهد؛ باربد)؛ (سعید درودی، بهزاد، مهتاب، 1372؛ در 152ص)؛ (عباس کرمیفر، تهران، ارغوان، 1372؛ در 160ص)؛ و (محمدمهدی فیاض، مشهد، نشر سنبله، 1379 در چهار جلد، رویای آلیس؛ ورود به سرزمین عجایب، دوستان جدید، دیدار با ملکه ستمگر)؛ (علی رحیم لو، تهران، دانشگر، 1380، 12ص)؛ (و «م‍ژده‌ خ‍س‍روان»؛ «ع‍ب‍اس‌ ن‍ع‍م‍ت‌ال‍ل‍ه‍ی»؛ «زه‍را ح‍ص‍ارپ‍رور»؛ «خانه ادبیات»؛ «م‍رت‍ض‍ی‌ ج‍دی‍دی»؛ و بسیاری دیگر)؛ ...؛<br /><br /><b>اخطار جدی: اگر هنوز داستان را نخوانده اید، و میخواهید حتما خود آنرا بخوانید، لطفا ادامه ی متن را نخوانید</b><br /><br />چکیده داستان: «آلیس» دختر یک جهانگرد «چارلز کینگزلی» است؛ او در هفت سالگی، خواب سرزمین عجایب را میبیند، و به آنجا وارد میشود؛ سیزده سال بعد، «آلیس» برای ازدواج با «لرد هانریش»، به اجبار به یک مهمانی میرود، و با دنبال کردن یک خرگوش، به یک چاله ی ژرف سقوط میکند، و برای بار دوم، وارد سرزمین عجایب میشود؛ در آنجا درمییابد، که ملکه ی سرخ، علیه خواهر خویش، ملکه ی سفید، شورش کرده، و اوضاع سرزمین عجایب، به هم ریخته است؛ او باید شمشیر نورانی را، که در قصر ملکه سرخ است، به دست آورد، و با آن، سر اژدهای ملکه را، از تنش جدا کند؛ «آلیس»، در مسیرش، با موجودات بسیاری، از جمله «یک کرم ابریشم دانا»، که همیشه درحال قلیان کشیدن است، «یک گربه» که میتواند نامرئی شود، «یک موش»، و همینطور فردی به نام «کلاهدوز دیوانه» آشنا میشود؛ و با یاری آنها، شمشیر را به چنگ میآورد، و به قصر «ملکه سفید» میرود؛ روز نهایی فرامیرسد، و دو ملکه، با ارتشهای خود به میدان جنگ میروند؛ «آلیس» با اژدهای «ملکه سرخ»، میجنگد، و با شمشیرش، سر اژدها را، از تنش جدا میکند؛ ملکه سرخ شکست میخورد، و به همراه شوالیه ی خویش تبعید میشود؛ در پایان، «آلیس» که کارش را در سرزمین عجایب به پایان رسانده، با نوشیدن خون اژدها، دوباره به دنیای واقعی برمیگردد، و با ازدواج با «هانریش» مخالفت میکند؛ سپس به همراه دوست پدرش، رو به سوی رویای پدر خویش، که سفر به تمام نقاط جهان بود، میرود<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 16/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2164483848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164483848" />
    <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino"><img alt="Luca Ambrosino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523134271p2/53478239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164483848?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luca Ambrosino" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino">Luca Ambrosino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788858013939" href="/book/show/28411290-alice-nel-paese-delle-meraviglie">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164483848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7637236505752999271">English (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6324090.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_' title='Alice's Adventures in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a>) / Italiano<br/><br/><blockquote>«Alice was beginning to get very tired of sitting by her sister on the bank, and of having nothing to do: once or twice she had peeped into the book her sister was reading, but it had no pictures or conversations in it, “and what is the use of a book,” thought Alice, “ without pictures or conversations ?”»</blockquote><p>Right from the beginning and from the first assertion of Alice, we understand that her thoughts encapsulate hard truth that make us smile fo</p></span>
  <span id="freeText7637236505752999271" style="display:none">English (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6324090.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a>) / Italiano<br><br><blockquote>«Alice was beginning to get very tired of sitting by her sister on the bank, and of having nothing to do: once or twice she had peeped into the book her sister was reading, but it had no pictures or conversations in it, “and what is the use of a book,” thought Alice, “ without pictures or conversations ?”»</blockquote><p>Right from the beginning and from the first assertion of Alice, we understand that her thoughts encapsulate hard truth that make us smile for their hindsight. Alice is a little bit bored child that decides to follow a strange rabbit to its rabbit hole. However, the hole is pretty weird, there are a lot of cups, and pictures, and shelves...</p><p>The journey-dream in Wonderland as a metaphor for life contains multiple keys of interpretation. Probably the conflict between adults and children is the more direct topic of the novel, exacerbated by the crazy Wonderland where usual rules of manners are being overturned for the custom use of wacky characters. And children, chuckling and listening to the novel, several times are wondering: "What's going on?".</p><p>My daughter had a lovely time with this book. And whenever she's having fun, I'm having fun.</p><p>Vote: 9</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528784594i/25728051._SX540_.jpg" width="420" height="315" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>«Alice cominciava a sentirsi assai stanca di sedere sul poggetto accanto a sua sorella, senza far niente: aveva una o due volte data un'occhiata al libro che la sorella stava leggendo, ma non v'erano nè dialoghi nè figure, - e a che serve un libro, pensò Alice, - senza dialoghi nè figure?»</blockquote><p>Già dall'incipit e dalla prima delle tante affermazioni di Alice, capiamo che racchiudono in sè verità schiaccianti... fanno sorridere per quanto sono palesi. Alice è una bimba un pò annoiata che decide di seguire uno strano coniglio fin nella sua tana. Ma la tana è piuttosto bizzarra, ci sono tazze e quadri e scaffali e...</p><p>Il viaggio-sogno nel mondo delle meraviglie come metafora della vita, racchiude mille interpretazioni e molteplici chiavi di lettura. Quello che traspare in maniera più evidente è probabilmente il conflitto adulti-bambini, esacerbato dall'assurdo paese delle meraviglie, nel quale le usuali regole della buona educazione sono capovolte ad uso personalizzato dei suoi strambi personaggi. E i bambini che ascoltano il racconto di Alice più volte si chiedono sghignazzando: "che cosa sta succedendo?"</p><p>Mia figlia si è divertita molto. E quando lei si diverte io mi diverto.</p><p>Voto: 8</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="7637236505752999271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2391823575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391823575" />
    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391823575?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391823575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6535713597218582165"><b>"It's no use going back to yesterday, because I was a different person then"</b><br/><br/><u>3rd read:</u> The quote struck me as appropriate to the world we're living in now. Not only have we changed, but the world has changed in the last few days and weeks. I guess these kind of observations are what I get from reading Alice in Wonderland during a pandemic! That said, this reading (actually an audible reading from Scarlett Johansson who did a fantastic job) reinforced the timeless quality of Lewis Carroll's celebr</span>
  <span id="freeText6535713597218582165" style="display:none"><b>"It's no use going back to yesterday, because I was a different person then"</b><br /><br /><u>3rd read:</u> The quote struck me as appropriate to the world we're living in now. Not only have we changed, but the world has changed in the last few days and weeks. I guess these kind of observations are what I get from reading Alice in Wonderland during a pandemic! That said, this reading (actually an audible reading from Scarlett Johansson who did a fantastic job) reinforced the timeless quality of Lewis Carroll's celebrated adventure. I also recognized how many great quotes there are in this book. Had fun going back down the rabbit hole! <br /><br />---<br /><br />I'd read Lewis Carroll's Alice's Adventures in Wonderland a few years ago; however, I just felt like picking it up again and I'm glad I did. I don't know why, but I enjoyed Alice's observations and the humor more this time. There's also something that's fun and a bit surprising when we're reading something (like Peter Pan or The Wizard of Oz) we thought we knew really well (because we've been exposed to the stories for so long even if we haven't read the actual story). I know my ratings are always subjective based on when and where I've read a specific book. It's clear that I was ready to have fun down the rabbit hole! Changing my rating from 3 stars to 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6535713597218582165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3294712208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3294712208" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3294712208?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780007350827" href="/book/show/7929931-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=children-of-all-ages">children-of-all-ages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3294712208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17811734858646134281"><i>
  <b>
    <u>“If you knew Time as well as I do,’ said the Hatter, ‘you wouldn’t talk about wasting it. </u>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/>There are so many great things to say about this story. For me, as a work of fantasy, it is on par with <i>The Chronicles of Narnia,</i> <i>Peter Pan</i> and <i>The Wizard of Oz</i> in terms of its creative imagination. <br/> <br/>These stories seem to centre on the idea of escape, escape from a boring reality in which the protagonist enters a world of exciting, and sometimes terrifying, adventure as they walk away from their</span>
  <span id="freeText17811734858646134281" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <u>“If you knew Time as well as I do,’ said the Hatter, ‘you wouldn’t talk about wasting it. </u>
  </b>
</i><br><br>There are so many great things to say about this story. For me, as a work of fantasy, it is on par with <i>The Chronicles of Narnia,</i> <i>Peter Pan</i> and <i>The Wizard of Oz</i> in terms of its creative imagination. <br> <br>These stories seem to centre on the idea of escape, escape from a boring reality in which the protagonist enters a world of exciting, and sometimes terrifying, adventure as they walk away from their old mundane life. This is a popular trope and here it works very well, Alice jumps down a rabbit hole and enters a truly insane world that makes little sense. <br><br><b><i>“In another moment down went Alice after it, never once considering how in the world she was to get out again.”</i> </b><br><br>Of all the fantasy worlds that work around this idea, this is by far the most bizarre I have read about. To put in mildly, the things Alice encounters feel hallucinogenic as if the mind has conjured them up whilst being intoxicated. Because as strange as it all seems, there is always a touch of the real about them. And I think this is because Lewis Carroll draws on real life experiences to bring his world to life.<br><br>The Mad Hatter, of course, is the best example. Although he only plays a small role here, and the movie versions certainly capitalise on his colourful character, he still stands out within the narrative: his character is the most memorable part of the story. He is only referred to as that name once, and he never identifies with it, though the name is distinctively his.<br> <br><i>
  <b>“How puzzling all these changes are! I'm never sure what I'm going to be, from one minute to another.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587540036i/29335289._SX540_.png" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He is the embodiment of true madness: dementia. And I did a little research on him and the origins of his character. In Victorian society, hatters often went mad because of the hat making process. They handled chemicals that caused what we now identify as dementia. Prolonged exposure to such substances degraded their minds to such a degree. So, in a way, he embodies a little piece of history with his quirkiness.<br><br>So I had a lot of fun here. This was actually my first ever read of this story. I've seen the films but never actually picked this up, it's certainly a quaint piece of madness to brighten your day with its nonsensical nature. <br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sean.barrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>| <a href="https://twitter.com/ultra_vegan" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>| <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sean.ultra_vegan/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Insta</a>| <a href="https://york.academia.edu/SeanBarrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Academia</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17811734858646134281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2624184873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2624184873" />
    <a title="Ilse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22848274-ilse"><img alt="Ilse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452137711p2/22848274.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624184873?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilse" href="/user/show/22848274-ilse">Ilse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780735811669" href="/book/show/381058.Alice_in_Wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22848274-ilse?shelf=uk">uk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624184873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13842311369459424990"><a href='https://postimages.org/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544629772i/26734551._SY540_.jpg' alt='Alice-Wonderland12' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>“Well, I should like to be a <i>little</i> larger, sir,<br/>if you wouldn’t mind,” said Alice : “ three inches<br/>is such a wretched height to be.”<br/>“It is a very good height indeed !” said the<br/>Caterpillar angrily, rearing itself upright as it<br/>spoke (it was exactly three inches high).</i><br/><br/>Today, reading a friend’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179270163?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>review</a> on <b>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland & Through the Looking-Glass</b>, I searched the garden shed for an edition of Alice in Wonderland illustrated by <b>Lisbeth Zwerger</b> which I read ages ago, to have anothe</span>
  <span id="freeText13842311369459424990" style="display:none"><a href="https://postimages.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544629772i/26734551._SY540_.jpg" alt="Alice-Wonderland12" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>“Well, I should like to be a <i>little</i> larger, sir,<br>if you wouldn’t mind,” said Alice : “ three inches<br>is such a wretched height to be.”<br>“It is a very good height indeed !” said the<br>Caterpillar angrily, rearing itself upright as it<br>spoke (it was exactly three inches high).</i><br><br>Today, reading a friend’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179270163?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> on <b>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland &amp; Through the Looking-Glass</b>, I searched the garden shed for an edition of Alice in Wonderland illustrated by <b>Lisbeth Zwerger</b> which I read ages ago, to have another look at Zwerger’s marvellous illustrations. Sadly enough it has disappeared – I must have lent out my copy to a friend. So, heading for a revisit in the near future hoping for the book to return, in the meantime I cannot resist sharing some of Lisbeth Zwerger’s illustrations which I add to the book appetizer I wrote because a friend asked me so long ago.<br><br><a href="https://postimages.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544629772i/26734552._SY540_.jpg" alt="Alice-Wonderland8" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>’Ach, meneer, ik hoop dat u het niet erg vindt, maar ik zou graag iets groter zijn,' zei Alice. 'Tien centimeter is zo'n lengte van niks.' 'Het is juist een uitstekende lengte!' zei de Rups boos, terwijl hij zich onder het spreken oprichtte (hij was precies tien centimeter lang).</b>
</i><br><br><a href="https://postimages.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544629772i/26734554._SY540_.jpg" alt="Alice-Wonderland15" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Op een slaapverwekkende warme zomerdag zit Alice zich naast haar lezende zus aan de waterkant onnoemelijk te vervelen. Een vestimentair piekfijn uitgedost wit Konijn dat gehaast voorbijsnelt, prikkelt haar nieuwsgierigheid. Ze gaat het achterna en tuimelt zo via een schier eindeloze konijnenpijp onverhoeds in Wonderland, een magische wereld bevolkt met sprekende dieren. Naast het voeren van absurde conversaties met de vreemdsoortige wezens, heeft ze plots haar handen vol met een baby die eigenlijk een big blijkt te zijn. Bovendien krimpt of groeit Alice de hele tijd door in een halsbrekend tempo als ze aan koekjes of paddenstoelen knabbelt!<br><br><a href="https://postimages.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544629772i/26734553._SY540_.jpg" alt="Alice-Wonderland14" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Carroll schreef dit fantasievolle, fascinerende sprookje over een avontuurlijk klein meisje dat alert en spitsvondig omgaat met onalledaagse gebeurtenissen voor het tienjarige dochtertje van een vriend. Van dit speelse, ietwat griezelige en surrealistische verhaal las ik een heel mooie, door Lisbeth Zwerger prachtig geïllustreerde uitgave, die ik graag nog eens zou herlezen als de vriend aan wie ik ze uitleende er ooit aan zou denken ze terug te bezorgen. In de tussentijd is er nog altijd de <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h0JvF9vpqx8" rel="nofollow noopener">videoclip</a> van <b>Tom Petty</b> die zich door het verhaal liet inspireren. Of ik zou het, nu ik groot ben, in het Engels kunnen lezen. Of zou ik dan terug krimpen?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13842311369459424990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1980132690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1980132690" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1980132690?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780147515872" href="/book/show/24611820-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980132690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15445582931109847279">"We're all mad here"<br/><br/>I'm not going to insult your intelligence by giving a plot summary for this book as I think every person on the planet knows the premise. However, for the sake of completion and satisfying my OCD tendencies... Alice is a young girl who falls through a rabbit hole into a fantasy world, meeting lots of weird and peculiar characters. And that's it.<br/><br/>Well, the Mad Hatter isn't wrong. I started this book excited at the premise of reading a classic that I don't recall ever having rea</span>
  <span id="freeText15445582931109847279" style="display:none">"We're all mad here"<br /><br />I'm not going to insult your intelligence by giving a plot summary for this book as I think every person on the planet knows the premise. However, for the sake of completion and satisfying my OCD tendencies... Alice is a young girl who falls through a rabbit hole into a fantasy world, meeting lots of weird and peculiar characters. And that's it.<br /><br />Well, the Mad Hatter isn't wrong. I started this book excited at the premise of reading a classic that I don't recall ever having read before. Within about ten pages, my excitement had quickly waned. I've come to the conclusion that people who love this book must have fallen in love with the book as a child and therefore reading this book will trigger feelings of nostalgia and memories of childhood. Because I simply hated every minute of reading this book. I went to bed every night and would find myself procrastinating on my phone instead of getting stuck into my book like I normally would.<br /><br />I don't enjoy nonsense. I like things to be logical and follow some kind of structure... I guess that's the scientist in me. Of course, not everything can be logical in horror books etc, but this was like a different level of ridiculousness. Nothing made any sense, things were all over the place. We were just jumping around everywhere and I just wanted the experience to be over. If this book wasn't so short, I think it would have became a DNF for me.<br /><br />Oh, and Alice literally has to the sassiest, cheekiest, rudest little girl I've ever encountered in literature. What a brat. I just wanted to put her in her place for the entirety of the novel. Nope, I hate Alice.<br /><br />The only highlight for me was the illustrations, as they are simply beautiful. So I apologise to all lovers of Alice in Wonderland but it's just not for me. I'll give 1 star for the story as I just can't allow myself to give zero stars... and I'll give 1 star for the illustrations. So that's 2 stars out of 5 from me! And a reading experience I'd like to forget.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15445582931109847279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146078992" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146078992" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4319311-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403244713p2/4319311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146078992?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/4319311-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781904808169" href="/book/show/2647293-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4319311-james?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4319311-james?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4319311-james?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4319311-james?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4319311-james?shelf=victorian-literature">victorian-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146078992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14886883281337565125">Having just finished Alice in Wonderland, the first thing that occurs to me is that I wish I had read it years ago. I've known the story of Alice for years thanks to Disney and the Mad Hatter on Batman, but for some reason I didn't get around to reading this as a child. While I expected to like it, I never realized what a joy this book would be. <br/><br/>Carroll was a logician, so it should come as no surprise that he uses his expertise in that field to create many hilarious logical fallacies. But what i</span>
  <span id="freeText14886883281337565125" style="display:none">Having just finished Alice in Wonderland, the first thing that occurs to me is that I wish I had read it years ago. I've known the story of Alice for years thanks to Disney and the Mad Hatter on Batman, but for some reason I didn't get around to reading this as a child. While I expected to like it, I never realized what a joy this book would be. <br /><br />Carroll was a logician, so it should come as no surprise that he uses his expertise in that field to create many hilarious logical fallacies. But what interested me the most was the prose; I could talk for a long time of the clean, beautiful concision of Carroll's writing and of the brilliance of his word games and puns, which obviously influenced Vladimir Nabokov (who composed a Russian translation of Alice). The way in which Carroll's narrative voice addresses the absurd events reminded me of Kafka's Metamorphosis. Why some would reject the former's unique literary genius while praising the latter's can be explained by the snobbery of those who would reject a masterpiece simply because it's a "children' book."<br /><br />These things interested the adult reader in me, but Alice is really for children of all ages. Thanks to the animated movie, I knew the characters and I felt like I was being reunited with old friends. I especially felt this during the Mad Tea Party, which I think must rank among the most brilliant comic scenes in English literature. However, Alice proves that books for children need not be dumbed down or sentimentalized. There are some dark undercurrents to the excellent humor (The Queen is obsessed with beheading, to use just the most famous example). And the beautiful concluding paragraph is a startling, Shakespearean meditation on childhood, age, and eventual womanhood. I admit that was a wonderful surprise. And then of course there's the drug use of the caterpillar and Carroll's suggested pedophiliac obsession with young girls. But people who approach Alice as psychedelic literature or a creepy Lolita story, I think, miss the point. However, these questions do add to the depth of the reading experience.<br /><br />Alice in Wonderland is indeed a rare kind of book: one which can entertain and enlighten both the child and the adult. Carroll's glittering novel hasn't been dimmed in the slightest by time, something that can't be said of the works of many of his contemporaries. Alice's adventures will doubtless fascinate us for untold years to come. Now if you'll excuse me, I have to go listen to White Rabbit. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14886883281337565125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11176383416716286162" style="display:none">Alice In Wonderland is a particularly rich and whimsical story, with something new to discover in every reading.<br />Alice herself is quite a character, and is able to stand up for herself against the strange and seemingly illogical world of wonderland. I suspect it's a combination of the two. I like some of Alice's adventures - really, how could I not? - but Wonderland was always leaning a bit towards the negative side of bizarre for me.</span>

<div id="review_2777064887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2777064887" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2777064887?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/44803602-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=completist-book-club">completist-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2777064887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11840675130167199622">If I didn't already know the story and the basic plot points of Alice in Wonderland from movies, books, and other pop culture retellings, I think this book would have been very confusing. I didn't realize how short the Wonderland part of Alice's story is so, despite the bizarre writing, it was a pretty quick read. In fact, if you are really into fairy tales, I imagine this could be a one sitting book.<br/><br/>The intro to the book mentioned this being psychedelic fiction. Having grown up frequently seein</span>
  <span id="freeText11840675130167199622" style="display:none">If I didn't already know the story and the basic plot points of Alice in Wonderland from movies, books, and other pop culture retellings, I think this book would have been very confusing. I didn't realize how short the Wonderland part of Alice's story is so, despite the bizarre writing, it was a pretty quick read. In fact, if you are really into fairy tales, I imagine this could be a one sitting book.<br /><br />The intro to the book mentioned this being psychedelic fiction. Having grown up frequently seeing art with tie-dyed mushrooms and a hookah smoking caterpillar on top, I was already thinking this book was likely quite a trip. The surreal storylines, bizarre characters, and the consumption of substances by Alice to alter her reality definitely make this a trippy experience.<br /><br />This is one case where I think the movies (at least the ones I have seen) have done a pretty good job stream-lining the story to improve the delivery. The essence of each of Alice's adventures is usually captured perfectly with excessively trippy material edited perfectly so as to not lose the viewer. Not often you can say the movie is better than the book!<br /><br />In the end, it is another classic that I am very glad to have read. Did it blow me away? Not really. Will I be recommending it to others? Not likely. But, if you have always enjoyed the Alice fairy tell - enough to say that you are a fan - I think you have to check out the source material.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11840675130167199622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3597479882" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3597479882?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781904808169" href="/book/show/2647293-alice-s-adventures-in-wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3597479882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11038180934170636831"><b>A group read with my buddies. I am proud of the fact that I managed to bring one of them in, kicking and screaming (Hi, Elena!)</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603068641i/30256488._SX540_.jpg' alt='Crazy' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>"How doth the little crocodile<br/>Improve his shining tail,<br/>And pour the waters of the Nile<br/>On every golden scale!<br/>How cheerfully he seems to grin,<br/>How neatly spread his claws,<br/>And welcome little fishes in<br/>With gently smiling jaws!"</i><br/><br/>I wonder if there is any person calling himself/herself/itself a reader who has no clue about this book. In case you have not (for example as a result </span>
  <span id="freeText11038180934170636831" style="display:none"><b>A group read with my buddies. I am proud of the fact that I managed to bring one of them in, kicking and screaming (Hi, Elena!)</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603068641i/30256488._SX540_.jpg" alt="Crazy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>"How doth the little crocodile<br>Improve his shining tail,<br>And pour the waters of the Nile<br>On every golden scale!<br>How cheerfully he seems to grin,<br>How neatly spread his claws,<br>And welcome little fishes in<br>With gently smiling jaws!"</i><br><br>I wonder if there is any person calling himself/herself/itself a reader who has no clue about this book. In case you have not (for example as a result of living under a rock in a very remote location), the poem above should give a decent clue. I love it by the way. <br><br>In any way, a little girl Alice followed an unusual White Rabbit and fell down a rabbit hole populated by all kinds of strange creatures. The motto of that place most probably was, "You don't have to be crazy to be here, but it surely helps." Looks like the Cheshire Cat agrees:<br><i>“"Oh, you can't help that," said the Cat; "we're all mad here."”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603068281i/30256471._SX540_.png" alt="Cheshire Cat" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To give yet another idea about the story, it reminded me a Tex Avery cartoon The Cat That Hated People: the poor cat's adventures on the Moon are somewhat similar to Alice's:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603069150i/30256496.jpg" alt="Moon" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>At least the creatures in both places were equally bizarre. <br><br>The book was immensely popular at the time of publishing, it so much that the Queen of Britain requested next book written by the author delivered to her as soon as it is available. To her complete surprise she received a hardcore math one: the author was a well-known mathematician.<br><br>The influence of this tale is impossible to overestimate. It was quoted uncountable number of times by everybody and their brother. Speaking just about famous "curiousier and curiousier" if I limit myself just to fantasy, out of the top of my head I can name such big names as Roger Zelazny and Glen Cook using it in their works. The story itself was inspiration of equally countless number of retellings, unofficial sequels (including grimdark versions), etc. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603068427i/30256474._SX540_.jpg" alt="Return to Wonderland" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I like the book well enough when I was a child. I loved it when I read it as a mature adult. It does have plenty of layers only adults can understand. How is about the following short quote:<br><i>"How long is forever? Sometimes just one second"</i><br>For this reason I did not classify it as a simple children tale, it is closer to adult fantasy disguising itself as a former. <br><br>However I will not torture you with more quotes as the book is unique in the sense that you can randomly select any line of any page and it would be a safe bet it turns out to be quotable. Do not believe me? Try it yourself. <br><br>Lastly a bit of sad and pathetic modern reality. In our obsession to sexualise every single thing we can think of, sometimes Lewis Carroll gets accused of being a pedophile - after all, his heroine was a little girl, thus he was sexually attracted to little girls. My personal view: I feel pity for miserable people trying to dig some dirt on anybody they can think of. Get a life! <br><br>P.S. I cannot think of any other book being harder to translate into another language. A long time ago I read two different translations and they felt like different stories: all the translations had to be adapted a lot from the original source to become comprehensible to non-English readers. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1603068721i/30256491._SX540_.jpg" alt="Translate" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11038180934170636831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4709859540419314517">You may have seen the Disney film or been to a play, but most everyone growing up in a Western European-based culture has had some contact in some form with Alice and her adventures. I cannot recommend high enough actually reading Lewis Carroll's superb book written for his daughter Alice's bedtime story. There is a lovely innocence to Alice and a startling and surprising freshness to all the creatures and characters she meets. It does sometimes feel like an acid trip, but then so does Charlie a</span>
  <span id="freeText4709859540419314517" style="display:none">You may have seen the Disney film or been to a play, but most everyone growing up in a Western European-based culture has had some contact in some form with Alice and her adventures. I cannot recommend high enough actually reading Lewis Carroll's superb book written for his daughter Alice's bedtime story. There is a lovely innocence to Alice and a startling and surprising freshness to all the creatures and characters she meets. It does sometimes feel like an acid trip, but then so does Charlie and the Chocolate Factory and other high flights of fancy. The great thing here is the oblique criticism of societal norms and the evocation of youth and innocence that is unforgettable and ageless. This is yet another book that one should read to their own kids as a gift for their imagination. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1950748002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1950748002" />
    <a title="Stacy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55502227-stacy"><img alt="Stacy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551527127p2/55502227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1950748002?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy" href="/user/show/55502227-stacy">Stacy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781433213656" href="/book/show/2495181.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950748002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3380104567878312757">I really enjoyed this, and being read by Michael York and a distinctive touch. <br/>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland is popularly known to many as a children's book, and Lewis Carroll admitted to writing it for the little girls of the Dean of the college he taught at. A quote from C. S. Lewis, in The Three Ways of Writing For Children (1952), "A children's story which is enjoyed only by children is a bad children's story. The good ones last, because a children's story is the best art-form for somethi</span>
  <span id="freeText3380104567878312757" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this, and being read by Michael York and a distinctive touch. <br />Alice's Adventures in Wonderland is popularly known to many as a children's book, and Lewis Carroll admitted to writing it for the little girls of the Dean of the college he taught at. A quote from C. S. Lewis, in The Three Ways of Writing For Children (1952), "A children's story which is enjoyed only by children is a bad children's story. The good ones last, because a children's story is the best art-form for something you have to say." Upon learning that there were other aspects of the book than simply just a children's story, I wanted to read it to see what those were. Alice's Adventures.... has been looked at in other ways over the years, determining there were many other elements employed into the story including:<br />1) satire of the corrupt judicial and political systems in Victorian England, as well as their abuse of power<br />2) satire of British imperialism and ethnocentrism<br />3) satire of social and cultural elements of Victorian society, such as its rigid educational system, social conventions, manners and etiquette<br /><br />Alice's Adventures in Wonderland has been examined in many ways: as an exploration of the mind and thought practices, with the aim of finding a hidden meaning dealing with math and logic (since Lewis was also a mathematician), even as a symptom of the use of drugs (which is interesting, give Lewis Carroll's favorite book was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/87635.Confessions_of_an_English_Opium_Eater" title="Confessions of an English Opium Eater by Thomas de Quincey" rel="nofollow noopener">Confessions of an English Opium Eater</a>, and there were many times I thought Lewis Carroll must have been tripping on some serious Laudanum when writing) and as a political satire/ analogy. Lewis Carroll was also known for his photography hobby. He is also known to say that he liked little children, except little boys. The fact that many photographs have been found in his collection with little girls scantily clad, and in various poses, including on his lap, and in light of his comment, have led some to believe that the book has references to pedophilia, but since he is not alive to defend himself, I will avoid that. <br />The original illustrator of Alice was Sir John Tenniel, who was a famous cartoonist for Punch Magazine, a periodical famous in Victorian England for its satire writing and cartoons. <br /><br />Since history is my thing, I was interested in the historical analogy. It is believed it is one of two entirely different analogies of two different eras, and I can see where both make sense. They are the Victorian and The War of the Roses, or the English Civil War. The main characters in each analogy are as follows:<br />Victorian:<br /><br />Wonderland= Victorian England<br />Queen of Hearts= Queen Victoria<br />Alice= symbol of British colonization and ethnocentrism, imperialism<br />White Rabbit= new awareness, realization, the fact not everything is at it seems, or an overnervous minor political functionary, fearful of displeasing Queen Victoria, awed by people of power, concerned with appearances before superiors<br /><br />King of Hearts= Prince Albert<br />Caterpillar= guru with many metaphysical questions, which is interesting considering the British colonization of India<br />Mad Hatter= Benjamin Disraeli<br />Mock Turtle &amp; Gryphon= satires of college alumnus<br /><br />The War of The Roses, or English Civil War (this analogy attributed to C. W. Giles, 1928):<br /><br />Queen of Hearts= Queen Margaret<br />King of Hearts= Henry VI<br />Knave of Wonderland= Duke of York<br />Duchess= Eleanor, Duchess of Gloucester, or Duchess Margaretha Mattausch (who was considered the ugliest woman in history and whom Sir John Tenniel used her portrait as a basis for his illustration of "Duchess"<br /><br />Baby= Richard of Gloucester, who became Richard III<br />Cheshire Cat= Sir William Catesby, follower of Richard III, and speaker of the House of Commons<br />White King= Richard's elder brother, Edward IV<br />Mad Hatter= Warwick the Kingmaker; Mad Hatter is also identified as one of King Edward's messengers, Hatta<br />March Hare= King Edward's messenger, Haigha; also identified as impersonal Yorkist claim to throne based on descent from Mortimer, Earl of March, heir to Richard II<br /><br />Fall of Humpty Dumpty, attended by complete army of White King= horrible defeat of the Lancastrians at Toulton<br /><br />Tweedledum &amp; Tweedledee not referring to the War of The Roses, but instead to the ancient English kingdoms of Mercia and Wessex, which ceased their constant bickering to jointly resist the Danish "Raven", which is one of many references in Alice to earlier history, another which would be:<br />Father William and the Young Man= William the Conqueror and Rufus<br /><br />So whichever theory as to the deeper meaning of Alice and her adventures you would subscribe to, it is an enjoyable and fascinating read.<br /><br />To view Mischenko and Stacy's Alphabet Challenge for letter "A", visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twogalsandabook.com/">https://twogalsandabook.com/</a> !!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3380104567878312757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3532863748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3532863748" />
    <a title="Settare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13198822-settare"><img alt="Settare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590610257p2/13198822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3532863748?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Settare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Settare" href="/user/show/13198822-settare">Settare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140623369" href="/book/show/1898443.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=fantasy-speculative">fantasy-speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=british-irish">british-irish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3532863748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17659808905976901298">I used to dislike Alice's Adventures in Wonderland when I was a kid. It always felt too weird for my taste (I was more a fan of Roald Dahl's quirk rather than Lewis Carroll's). Recently, I wanted something escapist and fun to read at night, so I picked up Alice and read* one chapter every night before going to sleep. (*I listened to the audiobook with Christopher Plummer's magnificent narration while following along on the text, mainly to look at the illustrations). <br/><br/>I loved it. <br/><br/>There are volumes</span>
  <span id="freeText17659808905976901298" style="display:none">I used to dislike Alice's Adventures in Wonderland when I was a kid. It always felt too weird for my taste (I was more a fan of Roald Dahl's quirk rather than Lewis Carroll's). Recently, I wanted something escapist and fun to read at night, so I picked up Alice and read* one chapter every night before going to sleep. (*I listened to the audiobook with Christopher Plummer's magnificent narration while following along on the text, mainly to look at the illustrations). <br /><br />I loved it. <br /><br />There are volumes written on escapist fantasy tales and Carroll's classic, so I don't think I have anything new to add to the legacy of this book here. Some people try to take this book way too seriously and criticize it and take it to pieces, but I don't. I'm happy to have a book that can transport me into a world that doesn't make much sense and doesn't owe me any explanations.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“If there’s no meaning in it,’ said the King, ‘that saves a world of trouble, you know, as we needn’t try to find any. And yet I don’t know,’ he went on, spreading out the verses on his knee, and looking at them with one eye; ‘I seem to see some meaning in them, after all.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That's wonderful. This book is a curious little journey supposedly for kids, but also an escape for grown-ups. It's funny and lovely and cozy and bizarre and stupid and mischievous, but I can't help feeling that it has a very sad undertone. Carroll keeps reminding you, in every chapter, how mad and bizarre and irreverent everything is; if you're in the real world, it's tiresome, boring, overly rational, and not really wonderful. If you take refuge in psychedelics and hallucinogens, it's weird and nonsensical and you wouldn't want to stay in that fantasy world forever, either. Both worlds are their own kind of crazy and you have to come to terms with that. <br />That's what I take away from this book. And I love it. And I wonder what it'd be like to read it stoned.<br />I'm joking. <br />Or am I?<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“And yet you incessantly stand on your head –<br />  Do you think, at your age, it is right?’<br />‘In my youth,’ Father William replied to his son,<br />  ‘I feared it might injure the brain;<br />But, now that I‘m perfectly sure I have none,<br />  Why, I do it again and again.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />* I highly recommend the audiobook by Christopher Plummer. He is a wonderful narrator and has designed so many creative, unique, and distinctive voices for each character that takes the experience of reading <i>Alice</i> to a whole new level of awesome. <br />Although, he's given the Queen an angry German accent which somehow reminds me of Hitler, and I'm not sure if that is entirely okay. It's certainly funny but too stereotypical, perhaps. In spite of that, it's one of the best audiobook performances I've ever listened to.<br /><br />** Update: the initial rating was four but I haven't been able to get Alice out of my head for the past week. It should be upgraded to a solid five. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17659808905976901298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
